  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d2acbc1b-b3d2-4cb1-9aad-c3720214e3b6'
      });
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer1974461172831497629">The award-winning novel about being out, being proud, and being ready for something else . . . now in paperback.<br/><br/>Rafe is a normal teenager from Boulder, Colorado. He plays soccer. He's won skiing prizes. He likes to write.<br/><br/>And, oh yeah, he's gay.   <span id="freeText1974461172831497629" style="display:none">The award-winning novel about being out, being proud, and being ready for something else . . . now in paperback.<br /><br />Rafe is a normal teenager from Boulder, Colorado. He plays soccer. He's won skiing prizes. He likes to write.<br /><br />And, oh yeah, he's gay. He's been out since 8th grade, and he isn't teased, and he goes to other high schools and talks about tolerance and stuff. And while that's important, all Rafe really wants is to just be a regular guy. Not that GAY guy. To have it be a part of who he is, but not the headline, every single time.<br /><br />So when he transfers to an all-boys' boarding school in New England, he decides to keep his sexuality a secret -- not so much going back in the closet as starting over with a clean slate. But then he sees a classmate break down. He meets a teacher who challenges him to write his story. And most of all, he falls in love with Ben . . . who doesn't even know that love is possible.<br /><br /> This witty, smart, coming-out-again story will appeal to gay and straight kids alike as they watch Rafe navigate feeling different, fitting in, and what it means to be himself.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1974461172831497629" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/591710-my-question-for-you-all-is-what-are-your">My question for you all is what are your thoughts about this book in terms of identity? Obviously for a long time Rafe lost himself because he looked at his sexuality as the only aspect that defined him. Do you all think that this is a way of oppression in the LBGT community due to the idea that most heterosexual individuals don&#39;t look at their sexuality as a defining aspect to their identity?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">As someone who came out early, and back in the 90s, I can say that I completely understood where Rafe was coming from. Being openly gay or, really, ev<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">As someone who came out early, and back in the 90s, I can say that I completely understood where Rafe was coming from. Being openly gay or, really, even just perceived as gay, when you are in high school ends up being 90% of your identify whether you want it to be or not.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/560333-is-it-bad-to-be-just-yourself">is it bad to be just yourself ??</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_560333'><a id="like_count_community_question_560333" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/560333?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">2 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F16100972-openly-straight">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/48885256-rachel-wyne"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_100x100-6433b08cbe793211f55e184d39e84c4d.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/48885256-rachel-wyne">Rachel Wyne</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">No, it is not bad at all to 'just be yourself'. I believe that is the overall message that this book is trying to tell us. We see Rafe go through a co<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">No, it is not bad at all to 'just be yourself'. I believe that is the overall message that this book is trying to tell us. We see Rafe go through a confusing state when it comes to his identity and giving up labels, but in the progress he looses sight of who he really is. Him coming to grips with that toward the end of the reading really allows the reader to see how being true to yourself and allowing these different aspects make up who you are instead of defining you results in being happy with who you are!<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_1243873626" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1243873626" />
    <a title="Kai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788524-kai"><img alt="Kai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573562141p2/41788524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kai" href="/user/show/41788524-kai">Kai</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=underrated">underrated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=2015">2015</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1243873626" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17405128806812630587"><i>“You can be anything you want, but when you go against who you are inside, it doesn’t feel good.”</i><br/><br/>4.5/5 Stars<br/><br/>This was a (nearly) perfect read. I absolutely enjoyed reading <i> Openly Straight </i>. On one hand because I didn't have any expectations towards it and on the other hand because it exceeded them anway.<br/><br/>I was suprised to like this book so much. The LGBT+ book market is still growing and growing. It's hard to find a book in this category that is able to live up to the readers expectations or to s</span>
  <span id="freeText17405128806812630587" style="display:none"><i>“You can be anything you want, but when you go against who you are inside, it doesn’t feel good.”</i><br /><br />4.5/5 Stars<br /><br />This was a (nearly) perfect read. I absolutely enjoyed reading <i> Openly Straight </i>. On one hand because I didn't have any expectations towards it and on the other hand because it exceeded them anway.<br /><br />I was suprised to like this book so much. The LGBT+ book market is still growing and growing. It's hard to find a book in this category that is able to live up to the readers expectations or to say, is outstanding. This one, along with <i>Aristotle and Dante Discover the Secrets of the Universe</i>, is exceptional.<br /><br />One of the aspects that makes <i>Openly Straight</i> a great novel is the relatable main character. Rafe is not a stereotype. He lies, breaks his own promises, messes up. He is happy to belong with people, struggling to stand up to his friends when it comes to his own beliefs and he fears that he might not be accepted anymore if he does so. He, for a fictional character, is very human and relatable.<br /><br />Something else that made this novel such an enjoyable read was the many emotions it brought up. It made me smile, giggle, laugh out loud. It made me read that line again and laugh even harder. It made me want to hug someone (Rafe/Ben!/the book/my pillow). It made me happy.<br /><br />The only thing that let me down was <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ the ending. I wanted a happy ending! I mean a happily ever after! Rafe and Ben! Together! Kissing! In Love! But yeah I understand why it did not end that way. But still... There is some hope left:  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />There will be a sequel from Ben's point of view which could not make me happier, since he's my favourite character. This also means, that there's the possibility of a future for Ben and Rafe. And I really want it to happen.<br /><br />I am now officially a fan of Bill Konigsberg!<br /><br /> <a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17405128806812630587" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1504993336" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1504993336" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1504993336?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=boarding-school">boarding-school</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1504993336" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12505653789368183955"><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16100972.Openly_Straight__Openly_Straight___1_' title='Openly Straight (Openly Straight, #1) by Bill Konigsberg' rel='nofollow noopener'>Openly Straight</a> is the story of Rafe, a teenager who is terribly tired of being labelled as the ‘‘gay guy’’ in his city, Boulder. Ergo, he decides to go to an all-boy boarding school and hide this part of himself. Not lie about it, just never mention it.<br/><br/>Except, he does lie. He invents himself a girlfriend, so he can avoid further inquisition from his jock group of friends on the matter of the heart. Rafe is pretty keen on not letting the truth about his sexual orientation slip out, especially no</span>
  <span id="freeText12505653789368183955" style="display:none"><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16100972.Openly_Straight__Openly_Straight___1_" title="Openly Straight (Openly Straight, #1) by Bill Konigsberg" rel="nofollow noopener">Openly Straight</a> is the story of Rafe, a teenager who is terribly tired of being labelled as the ‘‘gay guy’’ in his city, Boulder. Ergo, he decides to go to an all-boy boarding school and hide this part of himself. Not lie about it, just never mention it.<br /><br />Except, he does lie. He invents himself a girlfriend, so he can avoid further inquisition from his jock group of friends on the matter of the heart. Rafe is pretty keen on not letting the truth about his sexual orientation slip out, especially now that he’s made an extraordinary new masculine friend and has gotten closer to him than to anyone he’s ever met.<br /><br />Watching Rafe struggle and oppressing all his feelings for Ben seriously made my heart ache. I understood his reasons behind the act of not telling the truth, but it’s universally known that the truth always comes out, one way or the other, and I dreaded that moment. It is always only a matter of time.<br /><br />Even though Rafe seems fully okay with his sexual orientation for the most part of the story, the more it advances and we dig deep into his personality, the more we realize that he needs help accepting the whole ‘‘label’’ thing and not focusing all of his thoughts on that. At the end of the day, what other people see matters less than what we do. <br /><br />I wouldn’t exactly recommend this for those looking for a transcendent LGBT romance story, because the whole lying thing does have a negative effect on the atmosphere. But it’s a wonderful novel about acceptance and friendship. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12505653789368183955" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1907269442590199882">Rafe has already "come out" as being gay. His parents are very accepting, his friends do, and he even does not face bullying because of it.<br/>He just feels like he never truly gets to be a "normal" guy because everyone always sees him as "gay". <br/>So when he gets to go to boarding school he keeps his sexuality a secret.   <span id="freeText1907269442590199882" style="display:none">Rafe has already "come out" as being gay. His parents are very accepting, his friends do, and he even does not face bullying because of it.<br>He just feels like he never truly gets to be a "normal" guy because everyone always sees him as "gay". <br>So when he gets to go to boarding school he keeps his sexuality a secret. Not that he is ashamed. He just is tired of the labels.<br> <b>"Back in Boulder, when people saw me, they saw the GAY kid. It was like, every second of my life, I had to be aware of the fact that I was different."</b><br><a href="http://imgur.com/kViSPCx" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438867531ra/15764273.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Once he begins the school he realizes that labels happen to everyone after he joins the soccer team. Jock, goth, nerds, they all have labels attached to them.<br><a href="http://imgur.com/jaOuIqD" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438867531ra/15764274.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This book doesn't do the usual teenage angsty stuff, or at least for me it didn't. Rafe actually has a tad bit of sense in his head. Even if he does go the liar path.<br>I kept expecting the book to try and pull at my heartstrings.<br><a href="http://imgur.com/W2pXn7a" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438867531ra/15764275.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>It did, just not in the normal young adult book way. The main character Rafe knows that he is wrong in lying about himself, but he does it in a thoughtful way that makes you think throughout the whole book.<br>Interspersed throughout the book you have journal pages from Rafe that his teacher (who knows his secret) is grading. You see Rafe grow and change his mind on things that happen.<br>I think or rather hope that one day labeling people will stop. No one will stop and stare at two gay guys walking down the hall. That no one will think twice about that black guy over in men's clothing. <br><a href="http://imgur.com/mNxiDi7" rel="nofollow noopener">

Lean into the challenges, don't lean back. I don't always do it, but I love it."</b><br><br><i>Book source: Library</i></span>

<div id="review_600451482" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/600451482" />
    <a title="Susan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/739211-susan"><img alt="Susan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1335133091p2/739211.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/600451482?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susan" href="/user/show/739211-susan">Susan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer600451482" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6615492754381872512"><br/><b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/>I really, really, really loved this book (subtracted by) I’m really, really mad at this book. Leaves the total of I really loved this book. <br/><br/>Openly Straight is witty and clever and made me do the laugh-that-turns-into-a-chuckle-that-becomes-a-chortle-whiddled-down-to-a-smile-back-up-to-a-giggle-and-then-ends-with-a-sigh on more than one occasion! The writing is current and engaging and the story a new’ish take on the YA tale. The normal nerdy gay kid and the closeted jock were written in</span>
  <span id="freeText6615492754381872512" style="display:none"><br /><b>4.5 stars</b><br /><br />I really, really, really loved this book (subtracted by) I’m really, really mad at this book. Leaves the total of I really loved this book. <br /><br />Openly Straight is witty and clever and made me do the laugh-that-turns-into-a-chuckle-that-becomes-a-chortle-whiddled-down-to-a-smile-back-up-to-a-giggle-and-then-ends-with-a-sigh on more than one occasion! The writing is current and engaging and the story a new’ish take on the YA tale. The normal nerdy gay kid and the closeted jock were written in a refreshing way.<br /><br />Rafe has been growing up gay and out. He’s fully supported by his parents and his community. He’s an advocate for gay youth. But, he’s tired of the labels and decides to go start his junior year of high school at an all-boys boarding school…he also decides not to tell anyone he’s gay. He meets a variety of friends at school…all of whom play a role in your classic YA story, but again, in such a fun and creative way. And he falls in love with Ben, an is-he-straight-is-he-gay-is-he-bi-or-is-he-terrified jock…oh and one who loves philosophy and uses the word “perchance” in regular conversation (love this kid).<br /><br />Their friendship and their exploration of their feelings for one another were AWESOME. True, I’ve never met, and doubt I ever will meet, 2 more well-adjusted teenaged boys…EVER. But, I can suspend reality in order to be a part of their interactions and conversations that I adored. <br /><br />My anger towards this book is simply because of this: THAT’S THE END? REALLY????? I felt a little robbed. I get it…not all books need to be stamped with “The End”. I just prefer it. I want…I need to know what happens next. Grrrr…<br /><br />If you read and enjoyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/239092.Almost_Like_Being_in_Love" title="Almost Like Being in Love by Steve Kluger" rel="nofollow noopener">Almost Like Being in Love</a>, the quirky humor of Openly Straight has a similar feel. I thoroughly enjoyed myself and highly reco this book…<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6615492754381872512" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_645399748" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/645399748" />
    <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club"><img alt="Stacia (the 2010 club)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417661051p2/4013351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/645399748?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacia (the 2010 club)" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club">Stacia (the 2010 club)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Stacia (the 2010 club) by: </span>
      Buddy read with TBD girls
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=realistic-general-or-lit-fiction">realistic-general-or-lit-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer645399748" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4830894274238790420"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380425961i/850508.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>3.5 stars</b>. I'm curious if Bill Konigsberg ever sat at a lunch table with John Green and David Levithan. Why, you ask? I can't really quite put my finger on the why or how but I felt like Konigsberg was channeling some of the offbeat vibe that the other two authors have been known to use in their own style of writing.<br/><br/>Before you groan and say that all three authors are male, or have tackled writing about similar subjects, just hear me out. Or read me out, since you can't actually hear me saying an</span>
  <span id="freeText4830894274238790420" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380425961i/850508.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>3.5 stars</b>. I'm curious if Bill Konigsberg ever sat at a lunch table with John Green and David Levithan. Why, you ask? I can't really quite put my finger on the why or how but I felt like Konigsberg was channeling some of the offbeat vibe that the other two authors have been known to use in their own style of writing.<br><br>Before you groan and say that all three authors are male, or have tackled writing about similar subjects, just hear me out. Or read me out, since you can't actually hear me saying anything. <br><br><i>Openly Straight</i> just has this weirdly wonderful thing going on. It's funny, candid, and uncomfortable at times. Have we not seen this method of madness with Green or Levithan before? Yes? Okay, so maybe I'm not completely off-base.<br><br>Granted, <i>Openly Straight</i> stands on its own because the story is not one you see every day. I might have seen similar ideas before but not with the added bizarre personalities. Past similarities came with <i>Lifetime</i>-movie serious sadface moments. There were no dads karaoke-rapping or moms doing naked yoga. Rafe's parents reminded me of Gaylord (Greg) Focker's parents from <i>Meet the Fockers</i>. It's all I could picture, and it had me grinning inside of my head.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>I know that I need to close my window shades, unless I want to see a show that no son should see.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Can a gay kid pretend to be straight and get away with it? This is what we readers are here to find out. Rafe moves away to an all-boys school (odd choice, perhaps?) in order to get away from his "out" life in Boulder, CO, where everyone knows and labels him as the gay kid.<br><br>I get it. I really do. It's got to suck for people to see your sexual orientation instead of seeing you.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>So maybe being openly gay isn't a curse, but it's fucking exhausting.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>However, I sort of lost sympathy for Rafe after a while when he realized that he was badly deceiving everyone, and it wasn't going to be pretty when people found out. Yes, I get that the story has to go for x amount of pages and that you can't just spill the beans and be done with it, but maybe Rafe needed to be clueless just a little while longer, so I wouldn't be as frustrated with him for not wising up and dealing with reality. <br><br>But this was readable, and it was quirky, so I liked it. After all, where else are you going to read lines such as : <i>Are you, like, a Republican now too?</i> or <i>ground turkey that tasted like sadness</i>, or even <i>I have a long-standing agreement with cows that I won't eat their balls if they won't eat mine</i>?<br><br>While there's nothing new or life-changing between the pages and the message might have gotten to be a little too overzealous at times, when you got down to the heart of the matter, it's really all about someone needing to learn to love himself. That's a pretty familiar subject for most everyone. I think we've all been there at one point or another. Kudos to the author for tackling this tough subject with humor and sincerity.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4830894274238790420" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_728267084" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/728267084" />
    <a title="jv poore" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5157918-jv-poore"><img alt="jv poore" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570108420p2/5157918.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/728267084?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jv poore" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jv poore" href="/user/show/5157918-jv-poore">jv poore</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5157918-jv-poore?shelf=buried-under-books">buried-under-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5157918-jv-poore?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5157918-jv-poore?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5157918-jv-poore?shelf=adolescence">adolescence</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5157918-jv-poore?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer728267084" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14893523783862557472">I have been thinking about labels…..a lot. Sometimes, a label seems superfluous (the White girl), while other times it seems to be used as an “explanation” (the Blonde girl). On the other hand, the lack of a label could be seen as misleading (oh, you didn’t say he was a Jock). When, if ever, are labels genuinely applicable? <br/><br/>Openly Straight allows the main character, teen-aged Rafe, to search for an answer to this question. See, Rafe has an opportunity for a do-over. Because he is openly Gay, he </span>
  <span id="freeText14893523783862557472" style="display:none">I have been thinking about labels…..a lot. Sometimes, a label seems superfluous (the White girl), while other times it seems to be used as an “explanation” (the Blonde girl). On the other hand, the lack of a label could be seen as misleading (oh, you didn’t say he was a Jock). When, if ever, are labels genuinely applicable? <br /><br />Openly Straight allows the main character, teen-aged Rafe, to search for an answer to this question. See, Rafe has an opportunity for a do-over. Because he is openly Gay, he believes that he knows the perception and stigma that can accompany that label. He desperately wishes to know if he would be viewed differently without it. Will he find an answer, or will he find himself with even more complicated questions and fewer answers than he started with? Either way, it is a fabulously interesting journey on which we embark, as we accompany Rafe through his year of going from openly gay to slipping back into the closet….well, sort-of. <br /><br />Even in a relatively controlled experiment, all things won’t be equal. Rafe was The Gay Boy with no adverse affects in his charmingly indulgent Colorado town. He begins to question the wisdom of coming out. His acceptance into an East Coast boarding school seems to be the perfect opportunity for a fresh start. There is simply no way he could have anticipated the devastation that can accompany a perceived secret.<br /><br />Mr. Konigsberg tackles this somewhat sensitive topic head-on, honestly, and well…..openly. The characters are realistically flawed. They make mistakes, and don’t necessarily learn from them. The dialogues, relationships and rivalries are quintessential teen behaviors; while Rafe’s parents are affably atypical. Rafe’s story is certainly plausible; making his experiences feel very real to this reader. I had a vested interest in the outcome of his “experiment”. <br /><br />This book is amazingly written. Mr. Konigsberg brings up points that, despite my mulling, I had never considered. The most important thing that I learned from reading this book is that my issue isn’t with labels, it is with the stereo-typing that often accompanies the labels. I believe that this story translates well for any label, but I am afraid that the audience may be limited simply because the label in Rafe’s life is Gay, rather than Jock, or Geek. This is one time that I certainly hope I am mistaken, because this is a book that I believe any reader would enjoy. <br /><br /> This review was written for Buried Under Books Blog.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14893523783862557472" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_601157371" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/601157371" />
    <a title="Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas"><img alt="Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567953607p2/2018505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/601157371?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas">Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=read-on-kindle">read-on-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=own-electronic">own-electronic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=five-stars">five-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer601157371" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2913939229974554163"><b>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/>Is it every gay guy's duty to get out of the closet? Rafe doesn't want to deceive people, but he hates being "that one gay kid" back in his hometown. When he moves from Boulder, Colorado to an all-boys' boarding school in New England, he keeps his homosexuality a secret and pretends to like girls - soon enough, he's part of the jock pack, and he really likes it. But being openly straight isn't as easy as Rafe thinks, and he feels the pressure when he develops feelings for his teammate B</span>
  <span id="freeText2913939229974554163" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b><br /><br />Is it every gay guy's duty to get out of the closet? Rafe doesn't want to deceive people, but he hates being "that one gay kid" back in his hometown. When he moves from Boulder, Colorado to an all-boys' boarding school in New England, he keeps his homosexuality a secret and pretends to like girls - soon enough, he's part of the jock pack, and he really likes it. But being openly straight isn't as easy as Rafe thinks, and he feels the pressure when he develops feelings for his teammate Ben, who might be the only guy who really understands him.<br /><br />Rafe took awhile to grow on me, but about halfway through the novel I found myself rooting for him. Konigsberg addresses a multitude of real issues: the conflict between ingroups and outgroups, the effects of labeling, the importance of your sexuality in regard to your identity, and more. Konigsberg gives Rafe an honest voice to delve into these topics - his confusion and search for self never felt forced or scripted, and the second half of this novel almost pushed it to a 5-star rating. Contemporary YA fans will love <i>Openly Straight</i> for its quality writing and its quirky, fresh teenage perspective.<br /><br />I also adored the side characters in this novel. Rafe's friendship with Claire Olivia improved as the novel progressed, a great feat for a platonic relationship within a YA novel. Many people will appreciate the presence of Rafe's ultra-liberal parents; his bond with them and how it was sometimes strained but always loving made me smile. Rafe's relationship with Ben as a whole won me over with great speed - its development and denouement served as my favorite parts of the book. Their bromance triggered most of my fanboy-like squeals of joy.<br /><br />Overall, highly recommended for fans of realistic YA, glbt books, or a well-written teenage voice in general. One of my favorites of this year so far.<br /><br />*review cross-posted on my blog, <a href="http://thequietvoice18.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">the quiet voice</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2913939229974554163" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1083842914" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2294584289933409058"><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414515062i/11661824.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Dear friends,<br/>Look at the list of <b>literary awards</b> this book has been honoured with:<br/><b><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414497891i/11660153.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>Sid Fleischman Humor Award (2014)<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414497891i/11660153.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>Lambda Literary Award Nominee (2014)<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414497891i/11660153.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>Amelia Elizabeth Walden Award (ALAN/NCTE) Nominee (2014)<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414497891i/11660153.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>American Library Association Rainbow List (2014)<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414497891i/11660153.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>Texas Library Association's Tayshas List (Top Ten Title) (2014)<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414497891i/11660153.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>Georgia Peach Award Nominee (2014)<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414497891i/11660153.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>Yalsa's Best Fiction for Young Adults (2014)<br/></b><br/><br/>And then ask yourselves WHY FGS I HAVE NOT YET READ IT?! Though you don't have to do the same. It was ME</span>
  <span id="freeText2294584289933409058" style="display:none"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414515062i/11661824.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Dear friends,<br>Look at the list of <b>literary awards</b> this book has been honoured with:<br><b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414497891i/11660153.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">Sid Fleischman Humor Award (2014)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414497891i/11660153.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">Lambda Literary Award Nominee (2014)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414497891i/11660153.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">Amelia Elizabeth Walden Award (ALAN/NCTE) Nominee (2014)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414497891i/11660153.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">American Library Association Rainbow List (2014)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414497891i/11660153.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">Texas Library Association's Tayshas List (Top Ten Title) (2014)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414497891i/11660153.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">Georgia Peach Award Nominee (2014)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414497891i/11660153.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">Yalsa's Best Fiction for Young Adults (2014)<br></b><br><br>And then ask yourselves WHY FGS I HAVE NOT YET READ IT?! Though you don't have to do the same. It was ME who asked myself this question. It was ME who swallowed 336 pages in one sitting. It was ME who laughed highlighted laughed highlighted highlighted highlighted laughed smiled laughed highlighted highlighted highlighted highlighted dropped some tears laughed highlighted and then - WTF??!!<img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1414498240ra/11660170.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>I <b>ADORE</b> the first 90%. LOVELOVELOVE IT! I don't really know what to think about the last 10%. Right now I'm trying to find a reasonable explanation for that ending. Didn't this book win Sid Fleischman Humor Award? THE LAST 10% WAS NOT FUNNY! I read even the <i>Acknowledgements</i> and <i>About the author</i> at the end of the book searching for an explanation!<br><br><b>But one after another:</b><br><br>Rafe is a normal teenager from Boulder, Colorado. He plays soccer. He's won skiing prizes. He likes to write. And he is gay. Openly gay in Boulder, Colorado. His parents love him, his neighbours love him, he is a beloved 'gay kid' in Boulder, Colorado. <i>"But growing up in Boulder is like growing up in a bubble."</i> It's why he goes to Natick, an all-boys school, almost 3.000 miles away from his home town. He wants to start everything from the very beginning. <br><blockquote>
  <i>Finally, here it was. My chance for a do-over. Here at Natick, I could be just Rafe. Not crazy Gavin and Opal’s colorful son. Not the "different" guy on the soccer team. Not the openly gay kid who had it all figured out.</i>
</blockquote><br><br>He doens't plan to go back in the closet,he is just tired of feeling <i>different.</i> He decided to stop be open about it. He just wants to feel like one of the guys for once.<br><blockquote>
  <i>I was going to be label-free. Don’t ask, and I won’t tell. The only way I would actually lie was if I were asked directly, "Are you gay?" In that case, I’d say no. But even then I wouldn’t go on about being straight. I didn’t want to lie; I just wanted to not be the guy whose main attribute was liking other guys. Been there, done that.</i>
</blockquote><br>But how long can something like THIS stay unnoticeable? As he's fallen in love with Ben, a tiny insignificance of NOT-OPENLY-BEING-GAY turns into a BIG LIE. And <i>lying to a friend sucked.</i> Of course, he'll come to the point when he ought to tell the truth, when he has to stop to pretend to be someone else. Will it end good? <br><blockquote>
  <i>As soon as I tried to remove the label, a lie formed. In the end, that lie created a barrier way worse than the original one. How crazy is that? Ironic, I mean. I created a barrier getting rid of a barrier.</i>
</blockquote><br><br>It's soooooooo worth to read the book to find out what happened here. <br>So, read it and for now I shut my mouth.<br><br><b>The ending:</b><br><br>To all HEA-junkies: It is not a NOT-HEA. It is real. Like real life. I'd say that it is a good ending. So don't afraid to read it. Only...I was sure that I knew at around 50% already EXACTLY how the story would end, and I was OKAY with it. Because it is one of those book where "the journey is the reward". So, when suddenly I got the different ending from that I'd predicted, I was...<s>WTF?</s>surprised. <br>It was like a Disney Movie that suddenly becomes an open ending. <br>But I think that slowly I start to understand WHY the author did it. And I appreciate his courage and his way of thinking. <br><blockquote>
  <i><br>Can you just put a part of yourself on hold? And if you do, does it cease to be true? <br><br><br>How was I expecting to get closer to someone by not being truly me?<br></i>
</blockquote><br><b>The writing:</b><br><br>ABSOLUTELY FANTASTIC GREAT AMAZING FUNNY POIGNANT CLEVER WARM-HEARTED!<br>Great characters, witty, sweet, it goes straightly to my FAVOURITE shelf. NO HESITATION.<br><br>I utterly totally understand WHY this book has such a lot of literary awards. It is a literary juwel. A MUST READ. Better now than tomorrow.<br><br><br><b>Highly highly highly recommended!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="2294584289933409058" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_504665467" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/504665467" />
    <a title="Ami" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/134600-ami"><img alt="Ami" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485783876p2/134600.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/504665467?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ami" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ami" href="/user/show/134600-ami">Ami</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17934215-openly-straight">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/134600-ami?shelf=young-or-new-adult">young-or-new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/134600-ami?shelf=lgbtq-fiction">lgbtq-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/134600-ami?shelf=5-stars_rating">5-stars_rating</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer504665467" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17683682307900373299">Bill Konigsberg's first novel, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3040050.Out_of_the_Pocket' title='Out of the Pocket by Bill Konigsberg' rel='nofollow noopener'>Out of the Pocket</a>, was one of my earliest experiences with LGBT Young Adult -- and I loved it so very much. So I was so excited when I learned that Mr. Konisgberg was releasing his sophomore novel.<br/><br/>Seamus Rafael Goldberg (and no, none of his parents are Irish!) or Rafe is tired with being an openly gay kid in Boulder, Colorado. Rafe gets it easy, his hippie parents embrace him being gay and love him still. His mother is the president of PFLAG. His best friend, Clair</span>
  <span id="freeText17683682307900373299" style="display:none">Bill Konigsberg's first novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3040050.Out_of_the_Pocket" title="Out of the Pocket by Bill Konigsberg" rel="nofollow noopener">Out of the Pocket</a>, was one of my earliest experiences with LGBT Young Adult -- and I loved it so very much. So I was so excited when I learned that Mr. Konisgberg was releasing his sophomore novel.<br /><br />Seamus Rafael Goldberg (and no, none of his parents are Irish!) or Rafe is tired with being an openly gay kid in Boulder, Colorado. Rafe gets it easy, his hippie parents embrace him being gay and love him still. His mother is the president of PFLAG. His best friend, Claire Olivia, also doesn't mind. But at the same time, Rafe feels like it limits him. That he is seen only as "the gay kid" instead of "Rafe". So, in his new school in Natick, Massachusetts, Rafe decides that he wants to "<i>take a break</i>" from being gay.<br /><br />Except that it doesn't go exactly as he plans. Yes, at first Rafe enjoys the 'freedom' of being the 'normal' kid -- be part of the soccer posse, seen as a jock. But Rafe realizes that being a 'jock' is just a different label, with consequences that come with it. It becomes more difficult when Rafe likes this boy, Ben, and he cannot even be honest about himself.<br /><br />I really, REALLY love this story for being unique and refreshing and thoughtful. I love how it questions labels in society; that what is seen as 'good label' doesn't always mean positive (there is this kid, Robinson, who is not a stereotype gay, and he is tired of being seen as not gay, and he cannot wait to be able to "be gay"). I love all the characters and their different traits. I love the little project that the teacher gives Rafe to write a journal about himself, so he can assess himself and why he makes his choices.<br /><br />A couple of friends who did buddy read with me don't like the ending. I know that the ending seems to be, well, unfinished: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Rafe doesn't get the boy <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and that there is this sense of "<i>So what then</i>?" ... However, for me, it is perfect. <br /><br />Because when it comes to the journey of what he learns by being 'openly straight' in his first semester in Natick, Rafe gets it. He learns that trying to shed a label doesn't mean that he's free to do everything. Rafe learns that sometimes people who are looking at him might not really thinking <i>about</i> him. Rafe learns that trying to pass as normal (or what society thinks as normal) might not worth losing a part of himself, and that by lying to himself, he hurts others in process. <br /><br />And ... Rafe finally understands that he <i>can</i> stand still while the others are dancing. <b>Because being different, well, that is just another reason for celebration, isn't it?</b><br /><br />With this, Mr. Konigsberg, I can tell you that I am now a fan of yours. Thank you for this thoughtful story...<br /><br />PS: There's this tidbit about a gay quarterback who talks at Natick early in the book. While there's no name mentioned, isn't it wonderful if that quarterback turns out to be Bobby Framingham (from Out of the Pocket) :p</span>
  <a data-text-id="17683682307900373299" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1790364216" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1790364216" />
    <a title="prag ♻" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29249069-prag"><img alt="prag ♻" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598781220p2/29249069.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1790364216?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="prag ♻" class="user" itemprop="url" name="prag ♻" href="/user/show/29249069-prag">prag ♻</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to prag ♻ by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/53067638-crisanda-sapphire">Crisanda (Sapphire)</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29249069-prag?shelf=lgbtqiap-plus">lgbtqiap-plus</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29249069-prag?shelf=let-me-down">let-me-down</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1790364216" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5132970771063500337"><b>
  <blockquote>“It’s hard to be different,” Scarborough said. “And perhaps the best answer is not to tolerate differences, not even to accept them. But to celebrate them. Maybe then those who are different would feel more loved, and less, well, tolerated.”</blockquote>
</b><br/>There are two things you should know about this book:<br/><b>1. </b>Mr. Scarborough is the best character to ever exist.<br/><b>2. </b>It will take your beliefs apart, and question them.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>“We’re a pretty tolerant place,” Steve said, an edge to his voice.<br/>“Ah, interesting word. T</b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText5132970771063500337" style="display:none"><b>
  <blockquote>“It’s hard to be different,” Scarborough said. “And perhaps the best answer is not to tolerate differences, not even to accept them. But to celebrate them. Maybe then those who are different would feel more loved, and less, well, tolerated.”</blockquote>
</b><br />There are two things you should know about this book:<br /><b>1. </b>Mr. Scarborough is the best character to ever exist.<br /><b>2. </b>It will take your beliefs apart, and question them.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>“We’re a pretty tolerant place,” Steve said, an edge to his voice.<br />“Ah, interesting word. Tolerant. What does tolerant mean?”<br />“It means we tolerate,” Steve said, flat. “We accept people.” <br />“Actually, tolerance and acceptance are different. To tolerate seems to mean that there is something negative to tolerate, doesn't it? Acceptance, though, what's that?”<br />“Well, if you need to accept something, that means it's not like it should be, right? Like you accept something as it is. Acceptance is an affirmation you're good enough.”</b>
</blockquote><br />And in these two quotes, lies the crux of this novel. It doesn't tell us what to believe, the main character isn't preachy about anything. He's just trying to figure things out for himself. He's trying to understand labels, and why they're (not) important. And it's important that we, as readers, try to figure this out along with him. <br /><br />Rafe is tired of being the <b>gay kid</b>. He's tired of people expecting him to be different. Tired of people expecting him to be special. When someone else crossdresses on halloween - they're a travestite. When Rafe does the same - he's a drag queen. This book left me thinking about a hell lot of things. If being gay was the "norm", would we objectify men the way we talk about women as things? (We = society in general) Or is that treatment reserved only for women?<br /><br />Why do we have labels for everything?<br /><br /><b>
  <blockquote>"I'm so tired of being a type," I repeated. <br />"It's not just a black and white thing. Jock. Geek. Stoner. No one is considered just a human being, it seems like."</blockquote>
</b><br />I don't have the answers. Nor does <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1304838.Bill_Konigsberg" title="Bill Konigsberg" rel="nofollow noopener">Bill Konigsberg</a>. But it's important that we think about this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5132970771063500337" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1946361448" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1946361448" />
    <a title="Vanessa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36015922-vanessa"><img alt="Vanessa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1427283055p2/36015922.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1946361448?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vanessa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vanessa" href="/user/show/36015922-vanessa">Vanessa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780545798655" href="/book/show/23399202-openly-straight">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36015922-vanessa?shelf=ya-and-teen-books">ya-and-teen-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36015922-vanessa?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1946361448" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2721509227668609808">This is one of those 3 star ratings, that feel a bit weird, because I actually really enjoyed reading this book. It's way ahead in the entertainment level and quality of writing compared to quite a few other books on my 3 star list. <br/>There were just a few things that bothered me. Sure, you might say that every book has those and what are they compared to all the things you loved about it... but they just REALLY bothered me A LOT. They took me out of the story. <br/>(I also actually expect the sequel t</span>
  <span id="freeText2721509227668609808" style="display:none">This is one of those 3 star ratings, that feel a bit weird, because I actually really enjoyed reading this book. It's way ahead in the entertainment level and quality of writing compared to quite a few other books on my 3 star list. <br />There were just a few things that bothered me. Sure, you might say that every book has those and what are they compared to all the things you loved about it... but they just REALLY bothered me A LOT. They took me out of the story. <br />(I also actually expect the sequel to be awesome, so I'm totally prepared to rate it higher! Fingers crossed.)<br /><br />But before I start complaining, let me tell you what I liked first:<br /><br />- I thought Rafe was a totally believable teenage first person voice. From his perspective, he made perfect sense. He was wrong quite a lot of the time and said cringe worthy stuff, but he read as a real human teenager with lots of complicated things going on in his life. He wasn't always likeable, but teenage me kept nodding along with him, going "Jep, sounds familiar." in my head.<br /><br />- I also loved that at all times during this book, Rafe had other people important to him. He had a family, he had friends (and sort-of-friends) and he had a teacher he liked. Granted, the chapters were really short, but there were some where he just hung out with friends or talked to his mother and no love interest in sight. That was refreshing.<br /><br />- Ben was a great love interest. Give me all the love interests that are actually kind and decent people! Nice people can be sarcastic or snarky at times, too! <br /><br />- This book was funny. It honestly cracked me up quite a few times. I'm one of those readers who reads all books with the same stoic face. If a book makes me smile or laugh or even cry, it's always a feat and this book did the first two things more than once.<br /><br />So basically this book had humor, it had charme and it had some really nice characters... and here comes the big BUT:<br /><br />At first, I couldn't figure out if I was supposed to agree with Rafe's parents and his childhood friend at all. Most of the time, I figured I wasn't supposed to. I kept waiting for the moment where they went: "Wait a minute. Maybe we should take a step back here and try to understand Rafe better..." but it never happened, so I must assume that I was supposed to root for them all this time and just ... no?<br /><br />Yes, I get that Rafe's "Okay, I'm straight at this school and clearly nothing could go wrong." plan was bewildering. I get that especially his super liberal parents weren't the biggest fan of it. But how all three of his closest people reacted was just ... terrible? <br />The childhood friend reacted with such an anger, it was honestly so weird? She didn't even try to understand where Rafe was coming from. It was like he was insulting her personally.<br />And the parents? It was like they were defining themselves via their son's sexuality and were insulted that they couldn't be the 'parents to a gay son' anymore for like... one weekend? Just imagine your son asks you not to mention that he's gay for one weekend, while you're visiting the school. Should be easy right? Just don't ask your son if he has been (or thinking of) banging other dudes and you're fine. Ask him about his friends or about his classes. Talk to him about literally anything else. He's your son. You're close to each other. You can find other topics. <br />But Rafe's parents acted like it was the hardest thing in the world. It made me uncomfortable.<br />Not to mention that they were kind of creepy about their son's sexuality in general. Especially the mother... taking it in a stride that your son is gay is one (good) thing, but wishing for it is... eh? And then dragging him to all the PFLAG meetings he doesn't want to go to, become president of said group, buying him books he should read essentially like homework because 'one needs to know their own history' is just a tad too much. They and the childhood friend (Who says she has suuuch a good gaydar btw. Yikes.) honestly acted like screaming teenage slash fans.<br />It was like in trying to avoid the label, Rafe had to talk about his sexuality more than he usually had to (and it seems like he had to a lot before). It was a topic in every damn conversation he had with people from home. It was mindboggling.<br />Like damn, let your son try this thing. He's not doing drugs or out to murder people. You know and trust him, so let him figure himself out instead of repeating again and again who <i>you</i> think he is. Not to mention the guilt tripping about how "good" Rafe has it. Had he just been born 10 years earlier, he'd have suffered more! If his family/friends/town weren't so open, he'd have suffered more! Not everyone is as lucky as you, my gay son! <s>PRAISE US!</s><br />As funny and heartwarming as they were sometimes, they were honestly exhausting to read about. <br /><br />The other two things that I didn't love are tiny in comparison:<br />1. While I think that Ben was an excellent love interest, I thought the development was a bit lackluster. Rafe sees that Ben has kind eyes when they first meet, but actually thinks he's kind of a jerk? There is an awkward bathroom encounter, a less awkward party encounter and... suddenly they're close? And then suddenly even closer? I've seen better written development (But also worse.). And I was totally on Ben's side in the end.<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Rafe planned to do the 'lying by obmission' thing, but... he didn't. He started lying for real and he didn't stop once he and Ben got close enough to talk about sex and the like. It's one thing to lie to someone you're not close to, but Ben totally opened up to him. As soon as Rafe made up a lie about sleeping with a girl, I knew it wouldn't end well. I get why Rafe lied, but I also get why Ben was so hurt by it. His heart and head must have been a total mess and he ended up having sex with someone he was not on equal footing with. It's not unfixable, but I get why he needs time to think.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />(Another reason why I assume I'll like the sequel better is because all the feelings will already be in place.)<br />2. I didn't really like the resolution regarding the soccer team. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[So the experiment was a fail? A gay guy can't be friends with the popular jocks, because they're all jerks anyway? Why couldn't he keep at least some of his soccer friends? Someone who liked him just for himself? Are they really all just afraid of Steve or what? Then at least give us a hint that some of them still idk nod at him in the hallway or something. Or mention that he missed playing soccer at least. That was honestly a bummer. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I have lots of more thoughts about this book (ha, don't you like a book that makes you think?) but I don't know how to put them into coherent sentences. It was an enjoyable journey with one big roadblock. I'm nonetheless looking very much forward to the sequel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2721509227668609808" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_752162565" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/752162565" />
    <a title="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar"><img alt="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530646317p2/11183856.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/752162565?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly (and the Book Boar)" href="/user/show/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar">Kelly (and the Book Boar)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11183856-kelly-and-the-book-boar?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer752162565" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2504867100573058457">Find all of my reviews at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/'>http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br/><br/>Being gay isn’t a choice, but being out definitely is. Raised by some seriously hippie-dippie parents, Rafe’s coming out was a breeze. We’re talking the school held a special celebration, his mother became the president of the local PFLAG and Rafe began traveling to different schools in the area to mentor other kids. It was wonderful – until Rafe became JUST the gay guy. No one except his best friend, Claire Olivia, was interested in j</span>
  <span id="freeText2504867100573058457" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br><br>Being gay isn’t a choice, but being out definitely is. Raised by some seriously hippie-dippie parents, Rafe’s coming out was a breeze. We’re talking the school held a special celebration, his mother became the president of the local PFLAG and Rafe began traveling to different schools in the area to mentor other kids. It was wonderful – until Rafe became JUST the gay guy. No one except his best friend, Claire Olivia, was interested in just knowing HIM – they always wanted to know the GAY him. In an effort to shed all labels, Rafe transfers across the country to an all-boys boarding school. There he will play soccer, study hard in hopes of getting accepted to an Ivy league college and have a chance to just be Rafe. The plan of being “openly straight” and not discussing his sex life works out great, until he starts developing deeper feelings for one of his teammates.<br><br>Now let me tell you what I thought of this book:<br><br><a target="_blank" title="ImageShack - Image And Video Hosting" href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/13/nq1.gif/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1384552578ra/6901051.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><b>
  <i>“Did you know that LGBT kids are 8.4 times more likely than straight kids to attempt suicide? And 50 percent of LGBT kids are rejected by their parents? That between 20 and 40 percent of homeless teens say they’re gay, lesbian, or transgender, and that up to 50 percent of the guy teens have sold their bodies to support themselves?”</i>
</b><br><br>I have no idea if the above statement is true or not. It’s a quote from the book and the stats seem realistic. I can’t imagine how hard it must be to come out – to be labeled by many without them even getting to know you. That’s why books like <i>Openly Straight</i> resonate so deeply with me. This book pushes no agenda – it’s just what a romantic comedy YA book should be. It shows that characters are just like people and come in all varieties – gay, straight, funny, sympathetic, even vile. People are just people, a memorable character is a memorable character, a good author is a good author, and a good book is a good book. This is a good book. It was adorably funny and made me have some feely-feels too.<br><br><b>
  <i>“Perhaps the best answer is not to tolerate differences, not even to accept them. But to celebrate them. Maybe then those who are different would feel more loved, and less, well, tolerated.”</i>
</b><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="2504867100573058457" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer587930300" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6590493004592700206">In Openly Straight, Mr Konigsberg explores, among other things, labeling and stereotyping, identity and self-perception, and the triptych 'tolerance-acceptance-celebration' when it comes to difference/diversity.<br/><br/>The book is well-written, in a fresh and funny and a largely non-sententious way.<br/><br/>The thing is, though, I didn't like Rafe, the main character. I enjoyed certain parts of him, but I didn't really like him as a person and my opinion of him didn't improve in the last quarter of the book, eit</span>
  <span id="freeText6590493004592700206" style="display:none">In Openly Straight, Mr Konigsberg explores, among other things, labeling and stereotyping, identity and self-perception, and the triptych 'tolerance-acceptance-celebration' when it comes to difference/diversity.<br /><br />The book is well-written, in a fresh and funny and a largely non-sententious way.<br /><br />The thing is, though, I didn't like Rafe, the main character. I enjoyed certain parts of him, but I didn't really like him as a person and my opinion of him didn't improve in the last quarter of the book, either. I understand that to a certain degree, we all learn to navigate life by trial and error, and that he came out of the whole experience a better person, but that didn't help him come across as less of an impostor. <br /><br />Also, for me, if you took Rafe and his (extended) family aside, almost everything else in the story felt stereotypical. The jocks posse (which, of course, included at least one deeply closeted homosexual and at least one homophobic member,) the geeky roommate, the one openly gay student, the progressive English professor (who reminded me of Robin Williams in Dead Poets Society,) the unsophisticated sports coach, the love interest who couldn't take the step forward and come out as gay (or bi) because of all the things that held him back (mostly his family—naturally.)<br /><br />The book is about Rafe, so I understand why it had to end the way it did. Though I would have enjoyed it more had it been a dual POV story. That way, I could have spent some time in Ben's head, too, seen how he struggled with his own issues of identity and self-perception.<br /></span>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText14553386211722602045" style="display:none"><b>BR with Mishy!</b><br /><br />Rafe is an out and proud high school student who decides to go back into the closet because he's tired of being "the gay kid."
